## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv_dt = F(x, v, t)/m. The nonlinearity can arise from anharmonic restoring forces (e.g., Duffing), nonlinear damping (e.g., van der Pol), or combinations with external driving forces.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (polynomial restoring force)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x**2 * v (nonlinear damping)
- Driven harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * sin(c2 * t) (external periodic forcing)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (nonlinear + driving)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (damping + driving)
- Driven damped Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (full Duffing model)
- Driven Van der Pol: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x**2 * v + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (driven nonlinear damping)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order anharmonicity)
- Nonlinear damping variant: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- Coulomb + viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * x (mixed nonlinear terms)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * sin(c1 * t) (time-modulated stiffness)
- General quadratic: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x**2 + c3 * x * v + c4 * v**2 (second-order polynomial in x, v)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x┬│, xŌüĄ) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium ŌĆö use odd polynomial in x
- Nonlinear damping with amplitude dependence (e.g., x┬▓*v term) indicates energy-dependent dissipation as in van der Pol systems
- Periodic driving forces appear as sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) additive terms independent of state variables
- Parametric excitation appears as multiplicative coupling between x and sin(c*t), modulating effective stiffness
- If acceleration depends on t only through trigonometric functions, the system is periodically driven; if t appears linearly, consider secular drift
- Negative linear damping (positive coefficient on v) combined with nonlinear saturation (negative x┬▓*v) indicates self-sustained oscillation (limit cycle)
- Position-velocity product terms (x*v) can arise from coordinate-dependent damping or from expanding nonlinear force fields
